<p id="mwBI8">Immune organs vary by type of fish.<sup about="#mwt621" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-78" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-78"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-78" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 78;" id="mwBJA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBJE">[78]</span></a></sup> In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jawless_fish" title="Jawless fish" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJI">jawless fish</a> (lampreys and hagfish), true <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lymph" title="Lymph" id="mwBJM">lymphoid</a> organs are absent. These fish rely on regions of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lymphoid_tissue" title="Lymphoid tissue" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJQ">lymphoid tissue</a> within other organs to produce immune cells. For example, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Erythrocytes" title="Erythrocytes" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJU">erythrocytes</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Macrophages" title="Macrophages" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJY">macrophages</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Plasma_cells" title="Plasma cells" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJc">plasma cells</a> are produced in the anterior kidney (or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pronephros" title="Pronephros" id="mwBJg">pronephros</a>) and some areas of the gut (where <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Granulocytes" title="Granulocytes" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJk">granulocytes</a> mature.) They resemble primitive <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bone_marrow" title="Bone marrow" id="mwBJo">bone marrow</a> in hagfish. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cartilaginous_fish" title="Cartilaginous fish" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBJs">Cartilaginous fish</a> (sharks and rays) have a more advanced immune system. They have three specialized organs that are unique to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chondrichthyes" title="Chondrichthyes" id="mwBJw">Chondrichthyes</a>; the epigonal organs (lymphoid tissue similar to mammalian bone) that surround the gonads, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Leydig's_organ" title="Leydig's organ" id="mwBJ0">Leydig's organ</a> within the walls of their esophagus, and a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Spiral_valve" title="Spiral valve" id="mwBJ4">spiral valve</a> in their intestine. These organs house typical immune cells (granulocytes, lymphocytes and plasma cells). They also possess an identifiable <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thymus" title="Thymus" id="mwBJ8">thymus</a> and a well-developed <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Spleen" title="Spleen" id="mwBKA">spleen</a> (their most important immune organ) where various <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lymphocyte" title="Lymphocyte" id="mwBKE">lymphocytes</a>, plasma cells and macrophages develop and are stored. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Chondrostean" title="Chondrostean" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBKI">Chondrostean</a> fish (sturgeons, paddlefish, and bichirs) possess a major site for the production of granulocytes within a mass that is associated with the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Meninges" title="Meninges" id="mwBKM">meninges</a> (membranes surrounding the central nervous system.) Their heart is frequently covered with tissue that contains lymphocytes, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Reticular_cell" title="Reticular cell" id="mwBKQ">reticular cells</a> and a small number of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Macrophage" title="Macrophage" id="mwBKU">macrophages</a>. The chondrostean kidney is an important <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hemopoietic" title="Hemopoietic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBKY">hemopoietic</a> organ; where erythrocytes, granulocytes, lymphocytes and macrophages develop.</p>

<p id="mwBKc">Like chondrostean fish, the major immune tissues of bony fish (or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Teleostei" title="Teleostei" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBKg">teleostei</a>) include the kidney (especially the anterior kidney), which houses many different immune cells.<sup about="#mwt626" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-79" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-79"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-79" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 79;" id="mwBKk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBKo">[79]</span></a></sup> In addition, teleost fish possess a thymus, spleen and scattered immune areas within mucosal tissues (e.g. in the skin, gills, gut and gonads). Much like the mammalian immune system, teleost erythrocytes, neutrophils and granulocytes are believed to reside in the spleen whereas lymphocytes are the major cell type found in the thymus.<sup about="#mwt630" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-80" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-80"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-80" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 80;" id="mwBKs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBKw">[80]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt634" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-81" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-81"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-81" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 81;" id="mwBK0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBK4">[81]</span></a></sup> In 2006, a lymphatic system similar to that in mammals was described in one species of teleost fish, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Zebrafish" title="Zebrafish" id="mwBK8">zebrafish</a>. Although not confirmed as yet, this system presumably will be where naive (unstimulated) <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./T_cell" title="T cell" id="mwBLA">T cells</a> accumulate while waiting to encounter an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Antigen" title="Antigen" id="mwBLE">antigen</a>.<sup about="#mwt638" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-82" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-82"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-82" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 82;" id="mwBLI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBLM">[82]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBLQ">B and T lymphocytes bearing <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Immunoglobulin" title="Immunoglobulin" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBLU">immunoglobulins</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./T_cell_receptor" title="T cell receptor" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBLY">T cell receptors</a>, respectively, are found in all jawed fishes. Indeed, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Adaptive_immune_system" title="Adaptive immune system" id="mwBLc">adaptive immune system</a> as a whole <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Adaptive_immune_system#Evolution" title="Adaptive immune system" id="mwBLg">evolved</a> in an ancestor of all jawed vertebrates.<sup about="#mwt643" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-83" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-83"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-83" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 83;" id="mwBLk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBLo">[83]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="30" id="mwBLs"><h2 id="Conservation">Conservation</h2>
<p id="mwBLw">The 2006 <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature" id="mwBL0">IUCN</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List" id="mwBL4">Red List</a> names 1,173 fish species that are threatened with extinction.<sup about="#mwt656" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-84" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-84"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-84" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 84;" id="mwBL8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMA">[84]</span></a></sup> Included are species such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gadus_morhua" title="Gadus morhua" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBME">Atlantic cod</a>,<sup about="#mwt660" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-85" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-85"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-85" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 85;" id="mwBMI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMM">[85]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cyprinodon_diabolis" title="Cyprinodon diabolis" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBMQ">Devil's Hole pupfish</a>,<sup about="#mwt664" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-86" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-86"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-86" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 86;" id="mwBMU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMY">[86]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Coelacanth" title="Coelacanth" id="mwBMc">coelacanths</a>,<sup about="#mwt668" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-87" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-87"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-87" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 87;" id="mwBMg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMk">[87]</span></a></sup> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Great_white_shark" title="Great white shark" id="mwBMo">great white sharks</a>.<sup about="#mwt672" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-88" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-88"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-88" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 88;" id="mwBMs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBMw">[88]</span></a></sup> Because fish live underwater they are more difficult to study than terrestrial animals and plants, and information about fish populations is often lacking. However, freshwater fish seem particularly threatened because they often live in relatively small water bodies. For example, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Devil's_Hole_pupfish" title="Devil's Hole pupfish" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBM0">Devil's Hole pupfish</a> occupies only a single <span about="#mwt649" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"3"},"2":{"wt":"by"},"3":{"wt":"6"},"4":{"wt":"m"},"5":{"wt":"0"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBM4">3 by 6 metres (10 by 20</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt649"> </span><span about="#mwt649">ft)</span> pool.<sup about="#mwt650" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997449–450_89-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Helfman"},"2":{"wt":"Collette"},"3":{"wt":"Facey"},"4":{"wt":"1997"},"pp":{"wt":"449–450"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997449–450-89" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 89;" id="mwBM8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBNA">[89]</span></a></sup></p>

<section data-mw-section-id="31" id="mwBNE"><h3 id="Overfishing">Overfishing</h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBNI"><a href="./File:Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBNM"><img alt="Photo of shark in profile surrounded by other, much smaller fish in bright sunlight" resource="./File:Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg/220px-Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="2331" data-file-height="1074" data-file-type="bitmap" height="101" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg/330px-Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg/440px-Whale_shark_Georgia_aquarium.jpg 2x" id="mwBNQ"/></a><figcaption id="mwBNU"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Whale_shark" title="Whale shark" id="mwBNY">Whale sharks</a>, the largest species of fish, are classified as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Endangered_species" title="Endangered species" id="mwBNc">endangered</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt673" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Overfishing"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBNg"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt673" id="mwBNk">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Overfishing" title="Overfishing">Overfishing</a></div>

<p id="mwBNo">Overfishing is a major threat to edible fish such as cod and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tuna" title="Tuna" id="mwBNs">tuna</a>.<sup about="#mwt681" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-90" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-90"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-90" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 90;" id="mwBNw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBN0">[90]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt685" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-91" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-91"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-91" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 91;" id="mwBN4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBN8">[91]</span></a></sup> Overfishing eventually causes <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Population_dynamics_of_fisheries" title="Population dynamics of fisheries" id="mwBOA">population</a> (known as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish_stocks" title="Fish stocks" id="mwBOE">stock</a>) collapse because the survivors cannot produce enough young to replace those removed. Such <b id="mwBOI">commercial extinction</b> does not mean that the species is extinct, merely that it can no longer sustain a fishery.</p>

<p id="mwBOM">One well-studied example of fishery collapse is the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pacific_sardine" title="Pacific sardine" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBOQ">Pacific sardine</a> <i id="mwBOU">Sadinops sagax caerulues</i> fishery off the California coast. From a 1937 peak of <span about="#mwt686" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"790000"},"2":{"wt":"LT"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBOY">790,000 long tons (800,000</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt686"> </span><span about="#mwt686">t)</span> the catch steadily declined to only <span about="#mwt687" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"24000"},"2":{"wt":"LT"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBOc">24,000 long tons (24,000</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt687"> </span><span about="#mwt687">t)</span> in 1968, after which the fishery was no longer economically viable.<sup about="#mwt688" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997462_92-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Helfman"},"2":{"wt":"Collette"},"3":{"wt":"Facey"},"4":{"wt":"1997"},"p":{"wt":"462"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997462-92" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 92;" id="mwBOg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBOk">[92]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBOo">The main tension between <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fisheries_science" title="Fisheries science" id="mwBOs">fisheries science</a> and the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_industry" title="Fishing industry" id="mwBOw">fishing industry</a> is that the two groups have different views on the resiliency of fisheries to intensive fishing. In places such as Scotland, Newfoundland, and Alaska the fishing industry is a major employer, so governments are predisposed to support it.<sup about="#mwt698" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-93" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-93"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-93" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 93;" id="mwBO0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBO4">[93]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt702" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-94" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-94"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-94" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 94;" id="mwBO8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBPA">[94]</span></a></sup> On the other hand, scientists and conservationists push for stringent protection, warning that many stocks could be wiped out within fifty years.<sup about="#mwt706" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-95" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-95"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-95" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 95;" id="mwBPE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBPI">[95]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt710" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-96" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-96"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-96" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 96;" id="mwBPM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBPQ">[96]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="32" id="mwBPU"><h3 id="Habitat_destruction">Habitat destruction</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt711" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Environmental impact of fishing"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBPY"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt711" id="mwBPc">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Environmental_impact_of_fishing" title="Environmental impact of fishing">Environmental impact of fishing</a></div>

<p id="mwBPg">A key stress on both freshwater and marine ecosystems is habitat degradation including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Water_pollution" title="Water pollution" id="mwBPk">water pollution</a>, the building of dams, removal of water for use by humans, and the introduction of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Invasive_species" title="Invasive species" id="mwBPo">exotic</a> species.<sup about="#mwt715" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997463_97-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Helfman"},"2":{"wt":"Collette"},"3":{"wt":"Facey"},"4":{"wt":"1997"},"p":{"wt":"463"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997463-97" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 97;" id="mwBPs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBPw">[97]</span></a></sup> An example of a fish that has become endangered because of habitat change is the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pallid_sturgeon" title="Pallid sturgeon" id="mwBP0">pallid sturgeon</a>, a North American freshwater fish that lives in rivers damaged by human activity.<sup about="#mwt721" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-98" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-98"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-98" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 98;" id="mwBP4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBP8">[98]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="33" id="mwBQA"><h3 id="Exotic_species">Exotic species</h3>
<p id="mwBQE">Introduction of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Invasive_species" title="Invasive species" id="mwBQI">non-native</a> species occurs in many habitats. A notable case in point is the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea" id="mwBQM">Mediterranean Sea</a> which has become a major ‘hotspot’ of exotic invaders since the opening of the Suez Canal in 1869.  Since that time a thousand marine species of all sorts - fishes, seaweeds, invertebrates - originating from the Red Sea and more broadly from the Indo-Pacific have crossed the Canal from south to north to settle in the eastern Mediterranean Basin. Nowadays many of these tropical migrants, also called <b id="mwBQQ">Lessepsian species</b>, have extended their range towards the west, obviously favoured by the general warming of the Mediterranean. The resulting change in biodiversity is without precedent in human memory and is accelerating: a long-term cross-Basin survey engaged by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mediterranean_Science_Commission" title="Mediterranean Science Commission" id="mwBQU">Mediterranean Science Commission</a> recently documented <sup about="#mwt726" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-99" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-99"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-99" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 99;" id="mwBQY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQc">[99]</span></a></sup> that in just twenty years, from 2001 till 2021, no less than 107 alien fish species have reached the Mediterranean from both the tropical Atlantic and the Red Sea, which is more than the total recorded during the whole 130 preceding years. </p>

<p id="mwBQg">Another mode of introduction for marine species is transport across thousands of kms on ship hulls or in ballast waters. Examples abound of marine organisms being transported in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ballast_water_discharge_and_the_environment" title="Ballast water discharge and the environment" id="mwBQk">ballast water</a>, among them the invasive <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Comb_jelly" title="Comb jelly" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBQo">comb jelly</a> <i id="mwBQs">Mnemiopsis leidyi</i>, the dangerous bacterium <i id="mwBQw">Vibrio cholerae</i>, or the fouling <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel" id="mwBQ0">zebra mussel</a>. The Mediterranean and Black Seas, with their high volume shipping from exotic harbors, are particularly impacted by this problem.<sup about="#mwt728" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-100" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-100"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-100" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 100;" id="mwBQ4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBQ8">[100]</span></a></sup></p> 

<p id="mwBRA">Deliberate introductions of species with market potential are another frequent vector: one of the best studied examples is the introduction of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Nile_perch" title="Nile perch" id="mwBRE">Nile perch</a> into <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria" id="mwBRI">Lake Victoria</a> in the 1960s. Nile perch gradually exterminated the lake's 500 <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Endemism" title="Endemism" id="mwBRM">endemic</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cichlid" title="Cichlid" id="mwBRQ">cichlid</a> species. Some of them now survive in captive breeding programmes, but others are probably extinct.<sup about="#mwt734" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-101" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-101"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-101" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 101;" id="mwBRU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBRY">[101]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Carp" title="Carp" id="mwBRc">Carp</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Channidae" title="Channidae" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBRg">snakeheads</a>,<sup about="#mwt738" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-102" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-102"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-102" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 102;" id="mwBRk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBRo">[102]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tilapia" title="Tilapia" id="mwBRs">tilapia</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Perch" title="Perch" id="mwBRw">European perch</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Brown_trout" title="Brown trout" id="mwBR0">brown trout</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout" id="mwBR4">rainbow trout</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sea_lamprey" title="Sea lamprey" id="mwBR8">sea lampreys</a> are other examples of fish that have caused problems by being introduced into alien environments.</p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="34" id="mwBSA"><h2 id="Importance_to_humans">Importance to humans</h2>
<section data-mw-section-id="35" id="mwBSE"><h3 id="Economic">Economic</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt739" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Commercial fishing"},"2":{"wt":"Fishing industry"},"3":{"wt":"Aquaculture"},"4":{"wt":"Fish farming"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBSI"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt739" id="mwBSM">Main articles: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Commercial_fishing" title="Commercial fishing">Commercial fishing</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_industry" title="Fishing industry">Fishing industry</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">Aquaculture</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish_farming" title="Fish farming">Fish farming</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBSQ"><a href="./File:Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba,_DRC_(7609946524).jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBSU"><img alt="A row of square artificial ponds, with trees on either side" resource="./File:Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba,_DRC_(7609946524).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg/220px-Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" data-file-type="bitmap" height="147" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg/330px-Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg/440px-Community_fish-farming_ponds_in_the_rural_town_of_Masi_Manimba%2C_DRC_%287609946524%29.jpg 2x" id="mwBSY"/></a><figcaption id="mwBSc">These fish-farming ponds were created as a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cooperative" title="Cooperative" id="mwBSg">cooperative</a> project in a rural village.</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBSk"><a href="./File:Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBSo"><img resource="./File:Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg/220px-Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2477" data-file-type="bitmap" height="165" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg/330px-Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg/440px-Oulu_Market_Hall_20170617_04.jpg 2x" id="mwBSs"/></a><figcaption id="mwBSw">Fish counter display at the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Oulu_Market_Hall" title="Oulu Market Hall" id="mwBS0">Oulu Market Hall</a> in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Oulu" title="Oulu" id="mwBS4">Oulu</a>, Finland.</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwBS8">Throughout history, humans have used <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish_as_food" title="Fish as food" id="mwBTA">fish as a food source</a> for <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dietary_protein" title="Dietary protein" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBTE">dietary protein</a>. Historically and today, most fish harvested for human consumption has come by means of catching wild fish. However, fish farming, which has been practiced since about 3,500 BCE in ancient China,<sup about="#mwt747" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-103" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-103"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-103" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 103;" id="mwBTI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBTM">[103]</span></a></sup> is becoming increasingly important in many nations. Overall, about one-sixth of the world's protein is estimated to be provided by fish.<sup about="#mwt751" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Helfman_104-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Helfman"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Helfman-104"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Helfman-104" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 104;" id="mwBTQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBTU">[104]</span></a></sup> That proportion is considerably elevated in some <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Developing_nation" title="Developing nation" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBTY">developing nations</a> and regions heavily dependent on <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Seafood" title="Seafood" id="mwBTc">seafood</a>. In a similar manner, fish have been tied to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Primary_industry" title="Primary industry" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBTg">primary industry</a> and associated <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Food_industry" title="Food industry" id="mwBTk">food</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fodder" title="Fodder" id="mwBTo">feed</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry" id="mwBTs">pharmaceutical</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Secondary_industry" title="Secondary industry" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBTw">production</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Service_industries" title="Service industries" id="mwBT0">service industries</a>.</p>

<p id="mwBT4">Catching fish for the purpose of food or sport is known as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing" title="Fishing" id="mwBT8">fishing</a>, while the organized effort by humans to catch fish is called a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishery" title="Fishery" id="mwBUA">fishery</a> (which also describes the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_ground" title="Fishing ground" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBUE">area where such enterprise operates</a>). Fisheries are a huge global business and provide income for millions of people.<sup about="#mwt754" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Helfman_104-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Helfman"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Helfman-104" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 104;" id="mwBUI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBUM">[104]</span></a></sup> The annual yield from all fisheries worldwide is about 154 million tons,<sup about="#mwt758" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-105" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-105"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-105" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 105;" id="mwBUQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBUU">[105]</span></a></sup> with popular species including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herring" title="Herring" id="mwBUY">herring</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cod" title="Cod" id="mwBUc">cod</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Anchovy" title="Anchovy" id="mwBUg">anchovy</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tuna" title="Tuna" id="mwBUk">tuna</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Flounder" title="Flounder" id="mwBUo">flounder</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Salmon" title="Salmon" id="mwBUs">salmon</a>. However, the term fishery is broadly applied, and includes more organisms than just fish, such as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mollusca" title="Mollusca" id="mwBUw">mollusks</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crustacean" title="Crustacean" id="mwBU0">crustaceans</a>, which are often collectively called "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Shellfish" title="Shellfish" id="mwBU4">shellfish</a>" when used as food.</p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="36" id="mwBU8"><h3 id="Recreation">Recreation</h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBVA"><a href="./File:Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_(12968716714).jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBVE"><img resource="./File:Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_(12968716714).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg/220px-Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" data-file-type="bitmap" height="293" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg/330px-Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg/440px-Vendor_in_Fish_Market_-_Sylhet_-_Bangladesh_%2812968716714%29.jpg 2x" id="mwBVI"/></a><figcaption id="mwBVM">A <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bengalis" title="Bengalis" id="mwBVQ">Bengali</a> fish vendor from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sylhet" title="Sylhet" id="mwBVU">Sylhet</a></figcaption></figure>
<section data-mw-section-id="37" id="mwBVY"><h4 id="Fishkeeping">Fishkeeping</h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt759" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Fishkeeping"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBVc"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt759" id="mwBVg">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishkeeping" title="Fishkeeping">Fishkeeping</a></div>
<p id="mwBVk">Fish have been recognized as a source of beauty for almost as long as used for food, appearing in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cave_art" title="Cave art" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBVo">cave art</a>, being raised as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ornamental_fish" title="Ornamental fish" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBVs">ornamental fish</a> in ponds, and displayed in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aquarium" title="Aquarium" id="mwBVw">aquariums</a> in homes, offices, or public settings.</p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="38" id="mwBV0"><h4 id="Recreational_fishing">Recreational fishing</h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt762" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Recreational fishing"},"2":{"wt":"Angling"},"3":{"wt":"Fishing tournament"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBV4"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt762" id="mwBV8">Main articles: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Recreational_fishing" title="Recreational fishing">Recreational fishing</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Angling" title="Angling">Angling</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_tournament" title="Fishing tournament">Fishing tournament</a></div>
<p id="mwBWA"><i id="mwBWE">Recreational fishing</i> is fishing primarily for pleasure or competition; it can be contrasted with commercial fishing, which is fishing for profit, or <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Artisanal_fishing" title="Artisanal fishing" id="mwBWI">artisanal fishing</a>, which is fishing primarily for food. The most common form of recreational fishing is done with a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_rod" title="Fishing rod" id="mwBWM">rod</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_reel" title="Fishing reel" id="mwBWQ">reel</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fishing_line" title="Fishing line" id="mwBWU">line</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish_hook" title="Fish hook" id="mwBWY">hooks</a>, and any one of a wide range of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bait_(luring_substance)" title="Bait (luring substance)" id="mwBWc">baits</a>.  Recreational fishing is particularly popular in North America and Europe and state, provincial, and federal government agencies actively management target fish species.<sup about="#mwt770" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-106" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-106"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-106" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 106;" id="mwBWg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBWk">[106]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt774" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-107" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-107"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-107" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 107;" id="mwBWo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBWs">[107]</span></a></sup> Angling is a method of fishing, specifically the practice of catching fish by means of an "angle" (hook). Anglers must select the right hook, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cast_net" title="Cast net" id="mwBWw">cast</a> accurately, and retrieve at the right speed while considering water and weather conditions, species, fish response, time of the day, and other factors.</p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="39" id="mwBW0"><h3 id="Culture">Culture</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt775" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Fish in culture"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBW4"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt775" id="mwBW8">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish_in_culture" title="Fish in culture">Fish in culture</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBXA"><a href="./File:Matsya_painting.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBXE"><img alt="Photo of painting showing blue-skinned, 4-armed upper body of man standing in the opened mouth of a fish with bent tail with other, paler men facing him with hands raised together" resource="./File:Matsya_painting.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Matsya_painting.jpg/170px-Matsya_painting.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="977" data-file-type="bitmap" height="237" width="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Matsya_painting.jpg/255px-Matsya_painting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Matsya_painting.jpg/340px-Matsya_painting.jpg 2x" id="mwBXI"/></a><figcaption id="mwBXM"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Avatar" title="Avatar" id="mwBXQ">Avatar</a> of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vishnu" title="Vishnu" id="mwBXU">Vishnu</a> as a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Matsya" title="Matsya" id="mwBXY">Matsya</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBXc"><a href="./File:Goldfish_Matisse.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBXg"><img resource="./File:Goldfish_Matisse.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Goldfish_Matisse.jpg/170px-Goldfish_Matisse.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="531" data-file-height="800" data-file-type="bitmap" height="256" width="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Goldfish_Matisse.jpg/255px-Goldfish_Matisse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c1/Goldfish_Matisse.jpg/340px-Goldfish_Matisse.jpg 2x" id="mwBXk"/></a><figcaption id="mwBXo"><i id="mwBXs"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Goldfish_(Matisse)" title="Goldfish (Matisse)" id="mwBXw">Goldfish</a></i> by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse" id="mwBX0">Henri Matisse</a>, 1912, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pushkin_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Pushkin Museum of Fine Arts" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBX4">Pushkin Museum of Fine Arts</a>, Moscow</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwBX8">Fish themes have symbolic significance in many religions. In ancient <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia" id="mwBYA">Mesopotamia</a>, fish offerings were made to the gods from the very earliest times.<sup about="#mwt792" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_108-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBYE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBYI">[108]</span></a></sup> Fish were also a major symbol of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Enki" title="Enki" id="mwBYM">Enki</a>, the god of water.<sup about="#mwt793" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_108-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBYQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBYU">[108]</span></a></sup> Fish frequently appear as filling motifs in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cylinder_seal" title="Cylinder seal" id="mwBYY">cylinder seals</a> from the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./First_Babylonian_dynasty" title="First Babylonian dynasty" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBYc">Old Babylonian</a> (<abbr title="circa" about="#mwt785" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"circa","href":"./Template:Circa"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBYg">c.</abbr> 1830 BC – <abbr title="circa" about="#mwt786" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"circa","href":"./Template:Circa"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBYk">c.</abbr> 1531 BC) and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire" id="mwBYo">Neo-Assyrian</a> (911–609 BC) periods.<sup about="#mwt794" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_108-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBYs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBYw">[108]</span></a></sup> Starting during the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Kassites" title="Kassites" id="mwBY0">Kassite Period</a> (<abbr title="circa" about="#mwt787" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"circa","href":"./Template:Circa"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBY4">c.</abbr> 1600 BC – <abbr title="circa" about="#mwt788" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"circa","href":"./Template:Circa"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBY8">c.</abbr> 1155 BC) and lasting until the early <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire" id="mwBZA">Persian Period</a> (550–30 BC), healers and exorcists dressed in ritual garb resembling the bodies of fish.<sup about="#mwt795" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_108-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBZE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBZI">[108]</span></a></sup> During the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire" id="mwBZM">Seleucid Period</a> (312–63 BC), the legendary Babylonian <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Culture_hero" title="Culture hero" id="mwBZQ">culture hero</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Oannes_(mythology)" title="Oannes (mythology)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBZU">Oannes</a>, described by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Berossus" title="Berossus" id="mwBZY">Berossus</a>, was said to have dressed in the skin of a fish.<sup about="#mwt796" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-BlackGreen1992_108-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"BlackGreen1992"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-BlackGreen1992-108" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 108;" id="mwBZc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBZg">[108]</span></a></sup> Fish were sacred to the Syrian goddess <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Atargatis" title="Atargatis" id="mwBZk">Atargatis</a><sup about="#mwt800" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hyde2008_109-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hyde2008"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Hyde2008-109"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Hyde2008-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBZo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBZs">[109]</span></a></sup> and, during her festivals, only her priests were permitted to eat them.<sup about="#mwt801" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hyde2008_109-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hyde2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Hyde2008-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBZw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBZ0">[109]</span></a></sup></p>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBZ4"><a href="./File:Ichthus.svg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBZ8"><img resource="./File:Ichthus.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ichthus.svg/220px-Ichthus.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="902" data-file-height="445" data-file-type="drawing" height="109" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ichthus.svg/330px-Ichthus.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ichthus.svg/440px-Ichthus.svg.png 2x" id="mwBaA"/></a><figcaption id="mwBaE">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthys" title="Ichthys" id="mwBaI">ichthus</a> is a Christian symbol of a fish signifying that the person who uses it is a Christian.<sup about="#mwt804" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hyde2008_109-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hyde2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Hyde2008-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBaM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBaQ">[109]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt805" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Coffman2008_110-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Coffman2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Coffman2008-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwBaU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBaY">[110]</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwBac">In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Book_of_Jonah" title="Book of Jonah" id="mwBag">Book of Jonah</a>, a work of Jewish literature probably written in the fourth century BC, the central figure, a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Prophet" title="Prophet" id="mwBak">prophet</a> named <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jonah" title="Jonah" id="mwBao">Jonah</a>, is swallowed by a giant fish after being thrown overboard by the crew of the ship he is travelling on.<sup about="#mwt823" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherwood_111-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherwood"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Sherwood-111"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Sherwood-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwBas"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBaw">[111]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt827" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Ziolkowski2007_112-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Ziolkowski2007"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Ziolkowski2007-112"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Ziolkowski2007-112" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 112;" id="mwBa0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBa4">[112]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt831" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gaines_113-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gaines"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Gaines-113"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Gaines-113" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 113;" id="mwBa8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbA">[113]</span></a></sup> The fish later vomits Jonah out on shore after three days.<sup about="#mwt832" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sherwood_111-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sherwood"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Sherwood-111" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 111;" id="mwBbE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbI">[111]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt833" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Ziolkowski2007_112-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Ziolkowski2007"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Ziolkowski2007-112" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 112;" id="mwBbM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbQ">[112]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt834" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gaines_113-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gaines"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Gaines-113" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 113;" id="mwBbU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbY">[113]</span></a></sup> This book was later included as part of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible" id="mwBbc">Hebrew Bible</a>, or Christian <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Old_Testament" title="Old Testament" id="mwBbg">Old Testament</a>,<sup about="#mwt838" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-114" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-114"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-114" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 114;" id="mwBbk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbo">[114]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt842" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-115" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-115"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-115" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 115;" id="mwBbs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBbw">[115]</span></a></sup> and a version of the story it contains is summarized in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Surah" title="Surah" id="mwBb0">Surah</a> 37:139-148 of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Quran" title="Quran" id="mwBb4">Quran</a>.<sup about="#mwt846" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-116" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-116"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-116" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 116;" id="mwBb8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcA">[116]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBcE">Early Christians</a> used the <i id="mwBcI"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthys" title="Ichthys" id="mwBcM">ichthys</a></i>, a symbol of a fish, to represent Jesus,<sup about="#mwt847" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hyde2008_109-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hyde2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Hyde2008-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBcQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcU">[109]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt851" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Coffman2008_110-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Coffman2008"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Coffman2008-110"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Coffman2008-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwBcY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcc">[110]</span></a></sup> because the Greek word for fish, ΙΧΘΥΣ Ichthys, could be used as an acronym for "Ίησοῦς Χριστός, Θεοῦ Υἱός, Σωτήρ" (Iesous Christos, Theou Huios, Soter), meaning "Jesus Christ, Son of God, Saviour".<sup about="#mwt852" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Hyde2008_109-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Hyde2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Hyde2008-109" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 109;" id="mwBcg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBck">[109]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt853" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Coffman2008_110-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Coffman2008"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Coffman2008-110" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 110;" id="mwBco"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcs">[110]</span></a></sup> The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gospel" title="Gospel" id="mwBcw">gospels</a> also refer to "fishers of men"<sup about="#mwt854" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-117" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-117"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-117" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 117;" id="mwBc0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBc4">[117]</span></a></sup> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Feeding_the_multitude" title="Feeding the multitude" id="mwBc8">feeding the multitude</a>. In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dharma_(Buddhism)" title="Dharma (Buddhism)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBdA">dhamma</a> of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Buddhism" title="Buddhism" id="mwBdE">Buddhism</a>, the fish symbolize happiness as they have complete freedom of movement in the water.</p>

<p id="mwBdI">Among the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Deity" title="Deity" id="mwBdM">deities</a> said to take the form of a fish are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ika-Roa" title="Ika-Roa" id="mwBdQ">Ika-Roa</a> of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Polynesians" title="Polynesians" id="mwBdU">Polynesians</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dagon#Fish-god_tradition" title="Dagon" id="mwBdY">Dagon</a> of various ancient <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Semitic_people" title="Semitic people" id="mwBdc">Semitic peoples</a>, the shark-gods of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hawaii" title="Hawaii" id="mwBdg">Hawai<span typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Entity" about="#mwt860" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"okina","href":"./Template:Okina"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBdk">ʻ</span>i</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Matsya" title="Matsya" id="mwBdo">Matsya</a> of the Hindus. The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Astrology" title="Astrology" id="mwBds">astrological</a> symbol <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pisces_(astrology)" title="Pisces (astrology)" id="mwBdw">Pisces</a> is based on a constellation of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pisces_(constellation)" title="Pisces (constellation)" id="mwBd0">same name</a>, but there is also a second fish constellation in the night sky, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Piscis_Austrinus" title="Piscis Austrinus" id="mwBd4">Piscis Austrinus</a>.<sup about="#mwt859" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-118" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-118"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-118" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 118;" id="mwBd8"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBeA">[118]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBeE">Fish feature prominently in art and literature, in movies such as <i id="mwBeI"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Finding_Nemo" title="Finding Nemo" id="mwBeM">Finding Nemo</a></i> and books such as <i id="mwBeQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./The_Old_Man_and_the_Sea" title="The Old Man and the Sea" id="mwBeU">The Old Man and the Sea</a></i>. Large fish, particularly sharks, have frequently been the subject of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Horror_film" title="Horror film" id="mwBeY">horror movies</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thriller_(genre)" title="Thriller (genre)" id="mwBec">thrillers</a>, most notably the novel <i id="mwBeg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jaws_(novel)" title="Jaws (novel)" id="mwBek">Jaws</a></i>, which spawned a series of films of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)" id="mwBeo">same name</a> that in turn inspired similar films or parodies such as <i id="mwBes"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Shark_Tale" title="Shark Tale" id="mwBew">Shark Tale</a></i> and <i id="mwBe0"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snakehead_Terror" title="Snakehead Terror" id="mwBe4">Snakehead Terror</a></i>. Piranhas are shown in a similar light to sharks in films such as <i id="mwBe8"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Piranha_(1978_film)" title="Piranha (1978 film)" id="mwBfA">Piranha</a></i>; however, contrary to popular belief, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Red-bellied_piranha" title="Red-bellied piranha" id="mwBfE">red-bellied piranha</a> is actually a generally timid scavenger species that is unlikely to harm humans.<sup about="#mwt865" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-119" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-119"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-119" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 119;" id="mwBfI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBfM">[119]</span></a></sup> Legends of half-human, half-fish <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mermaid" title="Mermaid" id="mwBfQ">mermaids</a> have featured in folklore, including the stories of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hans_Christian_Andersen" title="Hans Christian Andersen" id="mwBfU">Hans Christian Andersen</a>.</p>

<div style="clear:both;" about="#mwt866" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"clear","href":"./Template:Clear"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBfY"></div>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="40" id="mwBfc"><h2 id="Terminology">Terminology</h2>
<section data-mw-section-id="41" id="mwBfg"><h3 id='"Fish"_or_"fishes"'><span id=".22Fish.22_or_.22fishes.22" typeof="mw:FallbackId"></span>"Fish" or "fishes"</h3>
<p id="mwBfk">Though often used interchangeably, in biology these words have different meanings. <i id="mwBfo">Fish</i> is used as a singular noun, or as a plural to describe multiple individuals from a single species. <i id="mwBfs">Fishes</i> is used to describe different species or species groups.<sup about="#mwt875" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Pauly2004_120-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Pauly2004"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Pauly2004-120"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-Pauly2004-120" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 120;" id="mwBfw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBf0">[120]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt879" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-121" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-121"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-121" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 121;" id="mwBf4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBf8">[121]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt869" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey19975_122-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Helfman"},"2":{"wt":"Collette"},"3":{"wt":"Facey"},"4":{"wt":"1997"},"p":{"wt":"5"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey19975-122" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 122;" id="mwBgA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgE">[122]</span></a></sup> Thus a pond would be said to contain 120 fish if all were from a single species or 120 fishes if these included a mix of several species. The distinction is similar to that between people and peoples.</p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="42" id="mwBgI"><h3 id='"True_fish"_or_"finfish"'><span id=".22True_fish.22_or_.22finfish.22" typeof="mw:FallbackId"></span>"True fish" or "finfish"</h3> <!-- Courtesy note per [[WP:RSECT]]: [[True fish]], [[Fin&#x2D;fish]] and [[Finfish]] redirect here -->
<ul id="mwBgM"><li id="mwBgQ">In biology, the term <i id="mwBgU">fish</i> is most strictly used to describe any animal with a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column" id="mwBgY">backbone</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gill" title="Gill" id="mwBgc">gills</a> throughout life, and limbs (if any) in the shape of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fin" title="Fin" id="mwBgg">fins</a>.<sup about="#mwt881" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson20062_23-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Nelson"},"2":{"wt":"2006"},"p":{"wt":"2"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson20062-23" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 23;" id="mwBgk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgo">[23]</span></a></sup> Many types of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aquatic_animal" title="Aquatic animal" id="mwBgs">aquatic animals</a> with common names ending in "fish" are not fish in this <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fish#Diversity" title="Fish" id="mwBgw">sense</a>; examples include <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Shellfish" title="Shellfish" id="mwBg0">shellfish</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cuttlefish" title="Cuttlefish" id="mwBg4">cuttlefish</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Starfish" title="Starfish" id="mwBg8">starfish</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crayfish" title="Crayfish" id="mwBhA">crayfish</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jellyfish" title="Jellyfish" id="mwBhE">jellyfish</a>. In earlier times, even biologists did not make a distinction<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwBhI"> </span>– sixteenth century natural historians classified also <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pinniped" title="Pinniped" id="mwBhM">seals</a>, whales, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibian" title="Amphibian" id="mwBhQ">amphibians</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodile" title="Crocodile" id="mwBhU">crocodiles</a>, even <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus" id="mwBhY">hippopotamuses</a>, as well as a host of aquatic invertebrates, as fish.<sup about="#mwt884" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-integrated_26-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"integrated"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-integrated-26" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 26;" id="mwBhc"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBhg">[26]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBhk">In fisheries, the term <i id="mwBho">fish</i> is used as a collective term, and includes <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mollusk" title="Mollusk" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBhs">mollusks</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crustacean" title="Crustacean" id="mwBhw">crustaceans</a> and any <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Aquatic_animal" title="Aquatic animal" id="mwBh0">aquatic animal</a> which is harvested.<sup about="#mwt889" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-fao_glossary_123-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"fao glossary"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-fao_glossary-123"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-fao_glossary-123" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 123;" id="mwBh4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBh8">[123]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mwBiA">The strict biological definition of a fish, above, is sometimes called a <i id="mwBiE">true fish</i>. True fish are also referred to as <i id="mwBiI">finfish</i> or <i id="mwBiM">fin fish</i> to distinguish them from other aquatic life harvested in fisheries or aquaculture.</li></ul>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="43" id="mwBiQ"><h3 id='"Shoal"_or_"school"'><span id=".22Shoal.22_or_.22school.22" typeof="mw:FallbackId"></span>"Shoal" or "school"</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt890" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Main","href":"./Template:Main"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Shoaling and schooling"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBiU"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt890" id="mwBiY">Main article: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Shoaling_and_schooling" title="Shoaling and schooling">Shoaling and schooling</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb mw:ExpandedAttrs" about="#mwt894" data-mw='{"attribs":[["alt",{"html":"alt=Photo of thousands of fish separated from each other by distances of &lt;span about=\"#mwt893\" typeof=\"mw:Transclusion\" data-parsoid=&apos;{\"pi\":[[{\"k\":\"1\"},{\"k\":\"2\"}]],\"dsr\":[107474,107490,null,null]}&apos; data-mw=&apos;{\"parts\":[{\"template\":{\"target\":{\"wt\":\"convert\",\"href\":\"./Template:Convert\"},\"params\":{\"1\":{\"wt\":\"2\"},\"2\":{\"wt\":\"in\"}},\"i\":0}}]}&apos;>2 inches (51&lt;/span>&lt;span typeof=\"mw:Entity\" about=\"#mwt893\" data-parsoid=&apos;{\"src\":\"&amp;amp;nbsp;\",\"srcContent\":\" \"}&apos;> &lt;/span>&lt;span about=\"#mwt893\" data-parsoid=\"{}\">mm)&lt;/span> or less","txt":"Photo of thousands of fish separated from each other by distances of 2 inches (51 mm) or less"}]]}' id="mwBic"><a href="./File:School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBig"><img alt="Photo of thousands of fish separated from each other by distances of 2 inches (51 mm) or less" resource="./File:School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg/220px-School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" data-file-type="bitmap" height="165" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg/330px-School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg/440px-School_of_Pterocaesio_chrysozona_in_Papua_New_Guinea_1.jpg 2x" id="mwBik"/></a><figcaption id="mwBio">These <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Goldband_fusilier" title="Goldband fusilier" id="mwBis">goldband fusiliers</a> are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Shoaling_and_schooling" title="Shoaling and schooling" id="mwBiw">schooling</a> because their swimming is synchronised.</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwBi0">An assemblage of fish merely using some localised resource such as food or nesting sites is known simply as an <i id="mwBi4">aggregation</i>. When fish come together in an interactive, social grouping, then they may be forming either a <i id="mwBi8">shoal</i> or a <i id="mwBjA">school</i> depending on the degree of organisation. A <i id="mwBjE">shoal</i> is a loosely organised group where each fish swims and forages independently but is attracted to other members of the group and adjusts its behaviour, such as swimming speed, so that it remains close to the other members of the group. <i id="mwBjI">Schools</i> of fish are much more tightly organised, synchronising their swimming so that all fish move at the same speed and in the same direction. Shoaling and schooling behaviour is believed to provide a variety of advantages.<sup about="#mwt895" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997375_124-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"sfn","href":"./Template:Sfn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Helfman"},"2":{"wt":"Collette"},"3":{"wt":"Facey"},"4":{"wt":"1997"},"p":{"wt":"375"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelfmanColletteFacey1997375-124" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 124;" id="mwBjM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBjQ">[124]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBjU">Examples:</p>
<ul id="mwBjY"><li id="mwBjc">Cichlids congregating at <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lek_(mating_arena)" title="Lek (mating arena)" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBjg">lekking</a> sites form an <i id="mwBjk">aggregation</i>.</li>
<li id="mwBjo">Many minnows and characins form <i id="mwBjs">shoals</i>.</li>
<li id="mwBjw">Anchovies, herrings and silversides are classic examples of <i id="mwBj0">schooling</i> fish.</li></ul>

<p id="mwBj4">The most common collective nouns for a group of fish in general are school and shoal. Both the words have evolved from the same common Dutch root 'schole' meaning a troop or crowd. While the words "school" and "shoal" have different meanings within biology, the distinctions are often ignored by non-specialists who treat the words as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Synonym" title="Synonym" id="mwBj8">synonyms</a>. Thus speakers of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./British_English" title="British English" id="mwBkA">British English</a> commonly use "shoal" to describe any grouping of fish, and speakers of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./American_English" title="American English" id="mwBkE">American English</a> commonly use "school" just as loosely.<sup about="#mwt902" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-125" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-125"}}'><a href="./Fish#cite_note-125" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 125;" id="mwBkI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBkM">[125]</span></a></sup></p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="44" id="mwBkQ"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="45" id="mwBk0"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" about="#mwt915" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Reflist","href":"./Template:Reflist"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBk4">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist   " about="#mwt915" id="mwBk8">
